      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Cleveland metropolitan area
       </b>
       , or
       <b>
        Greater Cleveland
       </b>
       as it is more commonly known, is the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       surrounding the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">
        Cleveland
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio" title="Northeast Ohio">
        Northeast
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">
        Ohio
       </a>
       , United States. According to 2016 United States Census estimates, the five-county
       <b>
        Cleveland–Elyria Metropolitan Statistical Area
       </b>
       (MSA) consists of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County,_Ohio" title="Cuyahoga County, Ohio">
        Cuyahoga County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Geauga_County,_Ohio" title="Geauga County, Ohio">
        Geauga County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_Ohio" title="Lake County, Ohio">
        Lake County
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lorain_County,_Ohio" title="Lorain County, Ohio">
        Lorain County
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Medina_County,_Ohio" title="Medina County, Ohio">
        Medina County
       </a>
       , and has a population of 2,055,612,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       making Greater Cleveland the 32nd
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">
        most populous metropolitan area
       </a>
       in the United States and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_census_statistical_areas" title="Ohio census statistical areas">
        largest metro entirely in Ohio
       </a>
       . Greater Cleveland is part of the larger
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland-Akron-Canton,_OH_Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Cleveland-Akron-Canton, OH Combined Statistical Area">
        Cleveland–Akron–Canton Combined Statistical Area
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megalopolis" title="Great Lakes Megalopolis">
        Great Lakes Megalopolis
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Changes in
       <a href="/wiki/House_price_index" title="House price index">
        house prices
       </a>
       for Greater Cleveland are publicly tracked on a regular basis using the
       <a href="/wiki/Case%E2%80%93Shiller_index" title="Case–Shiller index">
        Case–Shiller index
       </a>
       ; the statistic is published by
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        Standard &amp; Poor's
       </a>
       and is also a component of S&amp;P's 20-city
       <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">
        composite index
       </a>
       of the value of the U.S. residential real estate market.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio" title="Northeast Ohio">
        Northeast Ohio
       </a>
       refers to a similar but substantially larger area. This article covers the area generally considered to be Greater Cleveland, but includes some information generally applicable to the larger region, which is itself part of what is known historically as the
       <a href="/wiki/Connecticut_Western_Reserve" title="Connecticut Western Reserve">
        Connecticut Western Reserve
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Northeast_Ohio">
        Northeast Ohio
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Northeast Ohio">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio" title="Northeast Ohio">
        Northeast Ohio
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="662" data-file-width="626" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png/220px-Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png/330px-Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png/440px-Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cleveland_CSA_2013_v.3.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the Cleveland-Akron-Canton, Ohio CSA Based on 2013 U.S. Census Definitions
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Northeast Ohio consists of 16 counties (
       <a href="/wiki/Ashland_County,_Ohio" title="Ashland County, Ohio">
        Ashland
       </a>
       , Ashtabula,
       <a href="/wiki/Carroll_County,_Ohio" title="Carroll County, Ohio">
        Carroll
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Columbiana_County,_Ohio" title="Columbiana County, Ohio">
        Columbiana
       </a>
       , Cuyahoga, Geauga, Lake, Lorain,
       <a href="/wiki/Mahoning_County,_Ohio" title="Mahoning County, Ohio">
        Mahoning
       </a>
       , Medina, Portage,
       <a href="/wiki/Richland_County,_Ohio" title="Richland County, Ohio">
        Richland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stark_County,_Ohio" title="Stark County, Ohio">
        Stark
       </a>
       , Summit,
       <a href="/wiki/Trumbull_County,_Ohio" title="Trumbull County, Ohio">
        Trumbull
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Wayne_County,_Ohio" title="Wayne County, Ohio">
        Wayne
       </a>
       counties)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and includes the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">
        Akron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ashland,_Ohio" title="Ashland, Ohio">
        Ashland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ashtabula,_Ohio" title="Ashtabula, Ohio">
        Ashtabula
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Ohio" title="Brunswick, Ohio">
        Brunswick
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canton,_Ohio" title="Canton, Ohio">
        Canton
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">
        Cleveland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elyria,_Ohio" title="Elyria, Ohio">
        Elyria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lorain,_Ohio" title="Lorain, Ohio">
        Lorain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Ohio" title="Mansfield, Ohio">
        Mansfield
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Medina,_Ohio" title="Medina, Ohio">
        Medina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wadsworth,_Ohio" title="Wadsworth, Ohio">
        Wadsworth
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wooster,_Ohio" title="Wooster, Ohio">
        Wooster
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Warren,_Ohio" title="Warren, Ohio">
        Warren
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Youngstown,_Ohio" title="Youngstown, Ohio">
        Youngstown
       </a>
       . Northeast Ohio is home to approximately 4 million people, has a labor force of almost 2 million, and a gross regional product of nearly $170 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usmayors.org_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-usmayors.org-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other counties are sometimes considered to be in Northeast Ohio. These include
       <a href="/wiki/Erie_County,_Ohio" title="Erie County, Ohio">
        Erie
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Holmes_County,_Ohio" title="Holmes County, Ohio">
        Holmes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Huron_County,_Ohio" title="Huron County, Ohio">
        Huron
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tuscarawas_County,_Ohio" title="Tuscarawas County, Ohio">
        Tuscarawas
       </a>
       counties, and their inclusion makes the total population of the entire northeastern section of
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">
        Ohio
       </a>
       well over 4.5 million people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-census1-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Cities.2C_townships.2C_and_villages">

      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 United States Census
       </a>
       , the population was 2.077 million in the five-county MSA of the Greater Cleveland Area, making it the largest metropolitan-statistical area entirely within the state of Ohio.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 48.1% of the population was male and 51.9% were female. In 2010 the racial makeup of the five-county Area was 71.7% (1,490,074)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">
        Non-Hispanic Whites
       </a>
       , 19.7% (409,582)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Americans" title="Black Americans">
        Non-Hispanic Blacks or African Americans
       </a>
       , 0.2% (4,056)
       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
        American Indians and Alaskan Natives
       </a>
       , 2.0% (40,522)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
        Asian
       </a>
       (0.7%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_American" title="Indian American">
        Asian Indian
       </a>
       0.5%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_American" title="Chinese American">
        Chinese
       </a>
       0.2%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_American" title="Filipino American">
        Filipino
       </a>
       , 0.1%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">
        Korean
       </a>
       , 0.1%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_American" title="Vietnamese American">
        Vietnamese
       </a>
       , 0.1%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_American" title="Japanese American">
        Japanese
       </a>
       , 0.0% (398) Pacific Islander, 1.7% (35,224) from other races, and 2.0% (42,130) from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">
        two or more races
       </a>
       . 4.7% (98,133) of the population were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_or_Latino_American" title="Hispanic or Latino American">
        Hispanic or Latino of any race
       </a>
       (2.8%
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans_in_the_United_States" title="Puerto Ricans in the United States">
        Puerto Rican
       </a>
       , 1.0%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">
        Mexican
       </a>
       , 0.1%
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Americans" title="Dominican Americans">
        Dominican
       </a>
       , and 0.1%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">
        Cuban
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AkronSkylinewest.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1648" data-file-width="3296" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/AkronSkylinewest.jpg/220px-AkronSkylinewest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/AkronSkylinewest.jpg/330px-AkronSkylinewest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/AkronSkylinewest.jpg/440px-AkronSkylinewest.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AkronSkylinewest.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akron" title="Akron">
          Akron
         </a>
         , is the second largest city in the Greater Cleveland CSA.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The median income for a household in Greater Cleveland was $46,231 and the median income for a family, $59,611. The per capita income was $25,668. Persons living below the poverty line was 15.1%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According performed by Capgemini and the World Wealth Report by Merrill Lynch, the Cleveland area has nearly 54,000 millionaire household, and is expected to continue to grow at seventeen percent over the next five years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       For the past thirty years the Greater Cleveland area population has been in decline especially in terms of non-Hispanic whites all the while still being the most diverse region in the State.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But at the same time has become even more increasingly diverse as well. As of 2010 both the Hispanic and Asian population in the Cleveland-Akron-Ashtabula area grew by almost 40%, Hispanics now number at 112,307 (up from 80,738 in 2000).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And Asian alone accounts for 55,087 (up from 39,586 in 2000) but people who cite Asian and other ethnicites enumerate 67,231. The Chinese Americans are the oldest Asian group residing in Northeast Ohio, most visible in
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatown,_Cleveland" title="Asiatown, Cleveland">
        Cleveland's Chinatown
       </a>
       . Nevertheless, the area is also home to hundreds of Thais, Taiwanese, Pakistanis, Laotians, Cambodians, and Burmese peoples as well.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Cleveland area is also home to some of the nation's largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">
        Italian
       </a>
       (numbering over 205,000), Slavic, and Hungarian populations. The
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Ohioans" title="Hungarian Ohioans">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       population was so great at one time that Cleveland boasted of having the highest concentration of Hungarians outside of Budapest. Cleveland-Akron area is home to a large Slavic population (17.2% far higher than the nation's rate of 6%). The Greater Cleveland area is home to roughly 171,000 Polish, 38,000 Slovaks, 66,000 Slovenes 38,000 Czechs, 31,000 Russians, and 23,000 Ukrainians.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_Village" title="Slavic Village">
        Slavic Village
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaker_Square" title="Shaker Square">
        Shaker Square
       </a>
       once had some of the larger concentration in the city of Cleveland. Today, Slavic Village still continues to be home to many Slavic Ohioans. The Greater Cleveland area is home to the largest Slovak, Slovene, and Hungarian community in the world, outside of
       <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">
        Slovakia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
        Slovenia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition Slovenia maintains a Consulate-General in
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cleveland" title="Downtown Cleveland">
        Downtown Cleveland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city of Cleveland has also received visits from the Presidents of Hungary and Poland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Greater Cleveland is home to a sizable
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jews_and_Judaism_in_Cleveland" title="Jews and Judaism in Cleveland">
        Jewish community
       </a>
       . According to the North American Jewish Data Bank, an estimated 86,600 people or 3.0% as of 2011,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       above the nation's 1.7%, and up from 81,500 in 1996. The highest proportion in Cuyahoga County at 5.5% (of the county's total population). Today 23 percent of Greater Cleveland's Jewish population is under 17. Twenty-seven percent of Jewish people reside in The Heights (Cleveland Heights,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaker_Heights" title="Shaker Heights">
        Shaker Heights
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/University_Heights,_Ohio" title="University Heights, Ohio">
        University Heights
       </a>
       ). In 2010 nearly 2,600 people spoke
       <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">
        Hebrew
       </a>
       and 1,100
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" title="Yiddish language">
        Yiddish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">
        Ancestry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ancestry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The top largest ancestries in the Greater Cleveland MSA, were the following:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfinder2.census.gov_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-factfinder2.census.gov-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">
         German
        </a>
        : 20.4%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Slavic_Americans" title="Slavic Americans">
         Slavic
        </a>
        : 18.9% (8.2%
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_American" title="Polish American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_American" title="Slovak American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovene_American" title="Slovene American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_American" title="Czech American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_American" title="Russian American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_American" title="Ukrainian American">

        </a>
        , 1.0%
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Croatian_American" title="Croatian American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_American" title="Serbian American">

        </a>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rusyn_American" title="Rusyn American">

        </a>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Place_of_birth">
        Place of birth
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Place of birth">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Approximately 94.1% of the metropolitan area's population was native to the United States. Approximately 92.8% were born in the U.S. while 1.3% were born in
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._territory" title="U.S. territory">
        U.S. territory
       </a>
       , or born abroad to American parents. The rest of the population (5.9%) were foreign-born. The highest percentages of immigrants came from
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       (46.2%),
       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
        Asia
       </a>
       (32.7%),
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
        Latin America
       </a>
       (14.3%); smaller percentages of newcomers came from
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       (3.6%), other parts of
       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
        North America
       </a>
       (3.0%), and
       <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">
        Oceania
       </a>
       (0.3%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfinder2.census.gov_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-factfinder2.census.gov-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">
        American Community Survey
       </a>
       2006-2010, the number of Greater Cleveland area residents born overseas was 119,136 and the leading countries of origin were
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       (10,067),
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       (7,756),
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       (6,051),
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       (7,211),
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       (5,742),
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       (4,114),
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       (4,102),
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       (4,048),
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       (3,947),
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       (3,834),
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       (3,826), and
       <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">
        Yugoslavia
       </a>
       (3,820).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language_spoken_at_home">
        Language spoken at home
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Language spoken at home">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       is by far the most commonly spoken language at home by residents in the Cleveland-Akron-Elyria area; approximately 91.2% of the population over the age of five spoke only English at home.
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       speakers made up 2.8% of the population; speakers of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_languages" title="Asian languages">
        Asian languages
       </a>
       made up 1.1% of the population; speakers of other
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European languages
       </a>
       made up 3.9% of the population. Individuals who spoke languages other than the ones above represented the remaining 1.0% of the populace. As of 2011, individually in addition to English, 2.7% spoke
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , 0.6%
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , 0.5%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       , and 0.5%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States" title="Chinese language in the United States">
        Chinese
       </a>
       . 1.4% also spoke a
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic language
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2007, Cleveland area was home to the nation's 3rd highest proportion of
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian speakers
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Area_codes">
        Area codes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Area codes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In the 1950s,
       <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">
        AT&amp;T
       </a>
       assigned Greater Cleveland
       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_216" title="Area code 216">
        Area code 216
       </a>
       , which included all of
       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Ohio" title="Northeast Ohio">
        Northeast Ohio
       </a>
       . In 1996, Area code 216 was reduced in size to cover the northern half of its prior area, centering on Cleveland and its lake shore suburbs.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_330" title="Area code 330">
        Area code 330
       </a>
       was introduced for the southern half of Greater Cleveland, including
       <a href="/wiki/Medina_County,_Ohio" title="Medina County, Ohio">
        Medina County
       </a>
       . The western half of the region, including Ashland and Richland counties, and parts of Huron, Wayne, and Erie counties, are assigned
       <a href="/wiki/Area_codes_419_and_567" title="Area codes 419 and 567">
        area codes 419 and 567
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1997, area code 216 was further split as the need for additional phone numbers grew. Area code 216 was reduced in geographical area to cover the city of Cleveland and its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_suburbs" title="Inner suburbs">
        inner ring suburbs
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_440" title="Area code 440">
        Area code 440
       </a>
       was introduced to cover the remainder of was what previously area code 216, including all of
       <a href="/wiki/Lorain_County,_Ohio" title="Lorain County, Ohio">
        Lorain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Geauga_County,_Ohio" title="Geauga County, Ohio">
        Geauga
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_Ohio" title="Lake County, Ohio">
        Lake
       </a>
       counties, and parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County,_Ohio" title="Cuyahoga County, Ohio">
        Cuyahoga County
       </a>
       . Some communities, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Parma,_Ohio" title="Parma, Ohio">
        Parma
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Parma_Heights,_Ohio" title="Parma Heights, Ohio">
        Parma Heights
       </a>
       were divided between the 216 and 440 area codes. In 1999, Congressman
       <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Kucinich" title="Dennis Kucinich">
        Dennis Kucinich
       </a>
       introduced federal legislation to protect small and medium-sized cities from being split into two or more area codes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2000, it was anticipated that the available phone numbers in area code 330 would be exhausted, and an
       <a href="/wiki/Overlay_plan" title="Overlay plan">
        overlay area code
       </a>
       was introduced.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_234" title="Area code 234">
        Area code 234
       </a>
       was assigned to overlap existing area code 330. With the creation of area code 234, any new phone number in the geographical area formerly covered by area code 330 could be assigned a phone number in either the 234 or 330 area codes, with no change in local or long distance toll status. This made necessary the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Ten-digit_dialing" title="Ten-digit dialing">
        ten-digit dialing
       </a>
       within the 330/234 area code region. After the introduction of area code 234, assignments of new telephone numbers in the area did not continue at an accelerated pace, and new phone numbers for area code 234 were not assigned until 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In 2011 the Greater Cleveland area had a GDP of $134.4 billion (up from $130.7 billion in 2008), which would rank 57th
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">
        among countries
       </a>
       . Cleveland also has the twelfth highest merchandise value at $109.2 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usmayors.org_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-usmayors.org-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_industry">
        Business and industry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Business and industry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:From_Lakewood_Park.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="2048" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/From_Lakewood_Park.jpg/220px-From_Lakewood_Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/From_Lakewood_Park.jpg/330px-From_Lakewood_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/From_Lakewood_Park.jpg/440px-From_Lakewood_Park.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:From_Lakewood_Park.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">
          Lake Erie
         </a>
         and the
         <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Cleveland" title="Downtown Cleveland">
          Downtown Cleveland
         </a>
         skyline as seen from Lakewood Park, Lakewood.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Small_businesses_and_startups">
        Small businesses and startups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Small businesses and startups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Smaller_Enterprises" title="Council of Smaller Enterprises">
        Council of Smaller Enterprises
       </a>
       coordinates and advocates for small businesses in the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many of the area's
       <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">
        sustainability
       </a>
       -oriented companies are tied into the network
       <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurs_for_Sustainability" title="Entrepreneurs for Sustainability">
        Entrepreneurs for Sustainability
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
        Colleges and universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Greater Cleveland is home to a number of higher education institutions, including:

        </a>

         Case Western Reserve University
        </a>
        (

         Cleveland
        </a>
        )

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Greater Cleveland is served by international, regional and county airports, including:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burke_Lakefront_Airport" title="Burke Lakefront Airport">
         Burke Lakefront Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">
         Cleveland
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Concord_Airpark_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Concord Airpark Airport (page does not exist)">
         Concord Airpark Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Concord_Township,_Lake_County,_Ohio" title="Concord Township, Lake County, Ohio">
         Concord Township
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County_Airport" title="Cuyahoga County Airport">
         Cuyahoga County Airport
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Hopkins_International_Airport" title="Cleveland Hopkins International Airport">
         Cleveland Hopkins International Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">
         Cleveland
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lorain_County_Regional_Airport" title="Lorain County Regional Airport">
         Lorain County Regional Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russia_Township,_Lorain_County,_Ohio" title="Russia Township, Lorain County, Ohio">
         Russia Township
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willoughby_Lost_Nation_Municipal_Airport" title="Willoughby Lost Nation Municipal Airport">
         Willoughby Lost Nation Municipal Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Willoughby,_Ohio" title="Willoughby, Ohio">
         Willoughby
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Highway_notes">
        Highway notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Highway notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_271_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 271 (Ohio)">
         I-271
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Interstate_480_(Ohio)" title="Interstate 480 (Ohio)">
         I-480
        </a>
        are the only two three-digit interstates in the nation to be concurrent, near
        <a href="/wiki/Bedford_Heights,_Ohio" title="Bedford Heights, Ohio">
         Bedford Heights
        </a>
        in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_County" title="Cuyahoga County">
         Cuyahoga County
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">
        Public transit
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Public transit">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cleveland_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="Greater Cleveland Regional Transit Authority">
        Greater Cleveland Regional Transit Authority
       </a>
       operates a bus system and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland_Rapid_Transit" title="Cleveland Rapid Transit">
        heavy and light rail
       </a>
       in Cuyahoga County. Other transit agencies serve the surrounding counties and provide connections with RTA, including
       <a href="/wiki/Laketran" title="Laketran">
        Laketran
       </a>
       in Lake County, and
       <a href="/wiki/Lorain_County_Transit" title="Lorain County Transit">
        Lorain County Transit
       </a>
       in Lorain County. Cleveland's RTA Red Line which started in 1955, is the eighth oldest heavy rail rapid transit in the Country In 2007, RTA was named the best public transit system in North America by the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Public_Transportation_Association" title="American Public Transportation Association">
        American Public Transportation Association
       </a>
       , for "demonstrating achievement in efficiency and effectiveness."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Theater">
        Theater
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Theater">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Playhouse_Square_Center" title="Playhouse Square Center">
        Playhouse Square Center
       </a>
       is the epicenter of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland_Theater_District" title="Cleveland Theater District">
        Cleveland Theater District
       </a>
       and the second largest theater district in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Playhouse_Square_Theaters">
        Playhouse Square Theaters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Playhouse Square Theaters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="646" data-file-width="1016" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg/220px-Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg/330px-Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg/440px-Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Theater_Marquee.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the Ohio Theatre's marquee on Euclid Avenue, looking west. On the left is the Hanna building.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Allen_Theatre" title="Allen Theatre">
         Allen Theatre
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>

        </a>

         Palace Theatre
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kennedy%27s_Theatre" title="Kennedy's Theatre">
         Kennedy's
        </a>
        Cabaret
       </li>
       <li>
        Second Stage
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Helen_Lab_Theatre" title="The Helen Lab Theatre">
         The Helen Rosenfeld Lewis Bialosky Lab Theatre
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Westfield Insurance Studio Theatre
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In addition, Greater Cleveland has additional theaters throughout the region.
      </p>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cleveland is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Orchestra" title="Cleveland Orchestra">
        Cleveland Orchestra
       </a>
       , widely considered one of the finest
       <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">
        orchestras
       </a>
       in the world, and often referred to as the finest in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is one of the "
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Five_(orchestras)" title="Big Five (orchestras)">
        Big Five
       </a>
       " major orchestras in the United States. The Orchestra plays at
       <a href="/wiki/Severance_Hall" title="Severance Hall">
        Severance Hall
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/University_Circle" title="University Circle">
        University Circle
       </a>
       during the winter and at
       <a href="/wiki/Blossom_Music_Center" title="Blossom Music Center">
        Blossom Music Center
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Falls,_Ohio" title="Cuyahoga Falls, Ohio">
        Cuyahoga Falls
       </a>
       during the summer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city is also home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Pops_Orchestra" title="Cleveland Pops Orchestra">
        Cleveland Pops Orchestra
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Art">
        Art
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Art">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       There are two main
       <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">
        art museums
       </a>
       in Cleveland. The
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Museum_of_Art" title="Cleveland Museum of Art">
        Cleveland Museum of Art
       </a>
       is a major American art museum,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a collection that includes more than 40,000 works of art ranging over 6,000 years, from
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_art" title="Ancient art">
        ancient masterpieces
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">
        contemporary pieces
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Contemporary_Art_Cleveland" title="Museum of Contemporary Art Cleveland">
        Museum of Contemporary Art Cleveland
       </a>
       showcases established and emerging artists, particularly from the Cleveland area, through hosting and producing temporary exhibitions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_recreation">
        Sports and recreation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports and recreation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="1515" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg/300px-Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg/450px-Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg/600px-Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacobs_Field_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Field" title="Progressive Field">
          Progressive Field
         </a>
         , home of the
         <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">
          Cleveland Indians
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Cleveland's
       <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">
        professional sports
       </a>
       teams include the
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">
        Cleveland Indians
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">
        Cleveland Browns
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        National Football League
       </a>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers" title="Cleveland Cavaliers">
        Cleveland Cavaliers
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       ). The
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_County_Captains" title="Lake County Captains">
        Lake County Captains
       </a>
       , a Single-A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" title="Minor league baseball">
        minor league
       </a>
       affiliate of the Cleveland Indians, play in
       <a href="/wiki/Eastlake,_Ohio" title="Eastlake, Ohio">
        Eastlake
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Classic_Park" title="Classic Park">
        Classic Park
       </a>
       . Additionally, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie_Crushers" title="Lake Erie Crushers">
        Lake Erie Crushers
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Frontier_League" title="Frontier League">
        Frontier League
       </a>
       play at
       <a href="/wiki/Sprenger_Stadium" title="Sprenger Stadium">
        Sprenger Stadium
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Avon,_Ohio" title="Avon, Ohio">
        Avon
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Minor league hockey is represented in the area by the
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Monsters" title="Cleveland Monsters">
        Cleveland Monsters
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">
        American Hockey League
       </a>
       . They began play in the 2007–08 AHL season at the
       <a href="/wiki/Quicken_Loans_Arena" title="Quicken Loans Arena">
        Quicken Loans Arena
       </a>
       . The team is the top minor league affiliate of the
       <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Blue_Jackets" title="Columbus Blue Jackets">
        Columbus Blue Jackets
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        National Hockey League
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Metroparks" title="Cleveland Metroparks">
        Cleveland Metroparks
       </a>
       are a system of nature preserves that encircle the city, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_Valley_National_Park" title="Cuyahoga Valley National Park">
        Cuyahoga Valley National Park
       </a>
       encompasses the
       <a href="/wiki/Cuyahoga_River" title="Cuyahoga River">
        Cuyahoga River
       </a>
       valley between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" title="Cleveland, Ohio">
        Cleveland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Akron,_Ohio" title="Akron, Ohio">
        Akron
       </a>
       . The region is home to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mentor_Headlands_Beach_State_Park_(Ohio)" title="Mentor Headlands Beach State Park (Ohio)">
        Mentor Headlands Beach
       </a>
       , the longest natural beach on the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">
        Great Lakes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
